# ATM Bug and Optimization Backlog

This backlog captures ordinary ATM product/framework bugs, dogfood failures, workflow friction, and optimization ideas. It is not the release incident deny-list. Use `docs/INCIDENT_RESPONSE.md` and `known-bad-versions.json` only for published releases that can cause data loss, corrupt governance state, violate licensing constraints, or ship critical release-trust defects.

AI routing note: use `.agents/skills/atm-bug-backlog/SKILL.md` before writing backlog entries. The skill must first classify whether the issue belongs to ATM or to another project repo.

2026-07-11 follow-up:

- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-048` is now fixed by running cached onefile dist in-process instead of spawning a second Node process for every invocation. `npm run validate:next-warm-run-latency -- --json` passed on Windows with `cliLogicMs: 39`, warm-run `p50Ms: 1693.09`, `p95Ms: 5195.47`, and `wrapperOverheadMs: 1998.98`, all within the declared budgets. `npm run typecheck`, runner entrypoint regression, and frozen release build also passed.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-11-091` records the route friction found while starting this closeout: backlog IDs were treated as missing ledger task IDs by prompt-scoped `next`, then misrouted to `create-atom` by `start`.

Do not record non-ATM project bugs here. For adopter/app/game/site/data bugs, create or update `docs/governance/project-bug-and-optimization-backlog.md` inside the affected repo.

2026-07-09 sync note:

- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-09-059` is fixed by adding a read-only `ATM_NEXT_TASK_SCOPE_AUDIT_ADVISORY` route for missing task-like scope when `requestedAction` is `audit` or `analyze`; mutation-oriented missing scope remains fail-closed.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-047` was already fixed before this sync; `npm run validate:prompt-scoped-next` now covers broad all/open/remaining task-card prompts and confirms they route to the discovered batch queue instead of `ATM_NEXT_TASK_SCOPE_NOT_FOUND`.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-08-056` remains observable: after releasing and re-claiming a clean `ATM-FRAMEWORK-TEMP-codex-captain` lock, `doctor` / `tasks audit` can still report it as `stale-completed` with an old linked task even though the lock JSON no longer contains `linkedTaskId`. This is advisory and did not block `hook pre-push`, but it should be fixed before relying on stale-lock audit as a precise signal.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-08-056` is fixed by moving framework lock auto-reconcile audit records to `.atm/runtime/framework-lock-auto-reconcile.jsonl` and by preventing active unlabeled temp locks from inferring stale linked-task context from older actor sessions. Regression coverage lives in `validate:framework-development-governance` and `validate:task-ledger-governance`.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-045` / `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-053` are fixed by expanding `git commit` attempt status into a recoverable incident packet: every attempt now records HEAD before/after, whether HEAD advanced, `commit-status` and retry commands, raw copyable git command, and wrapper-staged residue rollback. The deadlock reason was that outer caller timeout or empty stdout/stderr left the operator unable to tell whether the commit had already landed, so retrying risked either duplicate work or manual index archaeology.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-09-060` is fixed by raising the governed `git commit` wrapper default timeout from 120s to 420s. The deadlock reason was that a normal framework pre-commit path took about 277s and passed, but the wrapper killed host git at 120s, reporting `ATM_GIT_COMMIT_TIMEOUT` even though the hook was not failing.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-043` is fixed at the commit-bundle preflight layer: a task with an active `closeout-only` claim now fails before auto-staging or pre-commit hooks when the bundle contains in-scope source mutations, returning `ATM_GIT_COMMIT_CLOSEOUT_ONLY_MUTATION` and the exact `next --claim --claim-intent write` recovery command.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-046`, `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-049`, and `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-050` were already fixed in the taskflow close atomicity lane: taskflow close commits now resolve actor-scoped git identity, commit from a temporary index, reset task-owned live-index residue after successful close commits, and share dry-run/write closeback-path readiness. The stale backlog rows were causing governance rework loops, so this sync marks the source-backed fixes as closed.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-08-056` is fixed by keeping framework lock auto-reconcile audit in `.atm/runtime/framework-lock-auto-reconcile.jsonl` instead of the protected history evidence singleton. This prevents `git commit --auto-stage` from picking up an uncommittable protected evidence file after same-actor stale temp-lock cleanup.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-047`, `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-052`, and `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-054` are fixed and verified: blanket all/open task-card prompts route to batch instead of `ATM_NEXT_TASK_SCOPE_NOT_FOUND`; protected override audit events survive/stage correctly; resumable validator runs expose status/resume behavior. The table rows were stale, so this sync removes three false High-priority governance blockers from the queue.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-06-15-008` is fixed by keeping cross-repo planning absolute paths out of Team Agents `file.write` leases: target repo write paths still require explicit target scope, while planning-repo absolute paths can route as read-only planning context without `ATM_TEAM_WRITE_SCOPE_TRAVERSAL`. Regression coverage lives in `node --strip-types scripts/validate-team-agents.ts --case permission-lease`.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-06-15-010` was already fixed by the historical-batch evidence lane: `evidence historical-batch` writes shared envelopes and task slices, and `taskflow close --historical-batch` consumes them with commit-range and close-readiness safeguards. The row was stale and is now synced to source reality.
- Dogfood note: this repair pass also showed a small workflow friction where the agent began a two-file quickfix after code localization before acquiring the framework temp claim. The claim was acquired immediately afterward and covered the touched files, but the root reason is that the fast playbook's "claim before edit" instruction is easy to miss once a bug is localized inside a large file. Keep improving `next`/skill UX so claim scope can be suggested from discovered candidate files before the first patch.
- Dogfood note: `ATM-BUG-2026-07-09-061` is fixed by adding `check:encoding:touched` and `check:encoding:staged` npm scripts backed by ATM's canonical `guard encoding` command. The touched wrapper includes untracked text files so newly created scripts/docs are checked before first staging.
- Dogfood note: `ATM-BUG-2026-07-09-062` is fixed by aligning the framework-maintenance fast playbook with the route command. The deadlock reason was that `next --prompt` correctly returned `framework-temp-claim-required` and a `framework-mode claim` command, but the embedded fast playbook still told agents to run `next --claim`, which fails with `ATM_NEXT_CLAIM_NO_TASK` when no imported task queue exists.
- Dogfood note: `ATM-BUG-2026-07-09-063` is fixed in this pass: `taskflow open --write` correctly fell back without a profile, but the recommended `tasks new --template aao-l2-split` path then failed because the framework runner had no bundled markdown template assets. The deadlock reason was that the documented low-level generator surface advertised a default template that could not be loaded in either frozen or source-first mode. The fix adds the default template asset to the markdown task-source package and locks source/frozen generation coverage in `tests/cli/tasks-new.test.ts`.
- Dogfood note: `ATM-BUG-2026-07-09-064` is fixed in this pass: `node atm.mjs git commit` can exceed a normal agent command timeout because its pre-commit hook runs heavyweight validators such as `validate:git-head-evidence`. The commit may still complete after the caller times out, so `git commit-status` now reports live branch commit queue diagnostics, including lock path, owner PID liveness, age, current HEAD, and wait-vs-inspect guidance.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-051` was already fixed in the emergency gate lane: `ATM_EMERGENCY_LANE_APPROVAL_REQUIRED` now includes required `--allowed-flag` entries for protected flags such as `--historical-delivery`, and the message warns that omitting them will later fail with `ATM_EMERGENCY_FLAG_NOT_APPROVED`. The stale row was keeping a resolved emergency-lane UX issue in the active queue.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-044` was already fixed in the prompt-scoped next lane: re-claim with escalated intent preserves scope-amended `claim.files` instead of rebuilding only from static task scope. The stale row was keeping a resolved claim lifecycle bug in the active queue.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-042` was already fixed in the prompt-scoped next validator: `teamPlanResult` is dumped only when assertions fail, so successful runs stay transcript-friendly. The stale row was keeping a resolved validator-noise issue in the active queue.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-09-059` was already fixed in the prompt-scoped next audit advisory lane: retrospective audit prompts that mention non-ledger historical labels now get `ATM_NEXT_TASK_SCOPE_AUDIT_ADVISORY` instead of the hard `ATM_NEXT_TASK_SCOPE_NOT_FOUND` blocker.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-06-15-004` is verified fixed in this pass: `taskflow close --historical-delivery` now supports the explicit operator waiver lane through `--waiver-out-of-scope-delivery --reason <text>` and the `--waive-out-of-scope` alias, while historical-delivery provenance records waived out-of-scope files and the waiver reason. The stale row kept a resolved closeback UX issue open; the proof path was briefly blocked by stale `taskflow-dryrun` assertions that still expected older commit-bundle/evidence behavior.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-055` is fixed by extending the taskflow close commit-bundle regression to cover stale staged bundle manifests: a same-task `.bundle-manifest.json` staged at an older version is reset out of the live index after the temp-index close commit lands the fresh version.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-06-16-014` is fixed by the historical-batch diagnostic disposition lane: partial or diagnostic-only slices can now be explicitly finalized as `keep-diagnostic`, `abandon`, or `remove-evidence`, while close-ready slices are refused and must still go through `taskflow close --historical-batch`.
- `ATM-BUG-2026-07-07-041` is fixed by deepening default `next` output compaction: non-verbose results now keep `evidence.nextAction` as the authoritative route payload, remove duplicated top-level aliases, keep playbook message echoes compact, and make `--verbose` a real parser-supported escape hatch for the full envelope.
- Dogfood note (2026-07-10 RFT batch `0002/0004/0005/0006/0007`): mechanical-split delivery friction, done-task import lockout, closeout exit-code ambiguity, and planning-index lag were recorded as `ATM-BUG-2026-07-10-076` through `ATM-BUG-2026-07-10-080`. Planning-mirror residue after successful closeback remains tracked in `ATM-BUG-2026-07-10-074`, with additional RFT cross-repo `source.planPath` evidence added in that row.

| ATM-BUG-2026-06-15-003 | 2026-06-15 | AI-Atomic-Framework | Bug | Medium | Fixed in TASK-TEAM-0029 / 48d5b55a | Git governance | Abandoned close did not open a close-commit-window, so follow-up governance commit could require emergency/no-verify paths even after close mutation succeeded. | Abandoned close should open a short-lived commit window covering the ledger/event artifacts that exist. | `TASK-APO-0029` abandoned cleanup required native `git commit --no-verify` after the ATM wrapper rejected the commit due to missing active work session. | Add validation that abandoned close can be committed through the ATM git wrapper without a fresh claim. |

| ATM-BUG-2026-06-15-005 | 2026-06-15 | AI-Atomic-Framework | Optimization | Medium | Fixed in 2026-06-28 onefile extraction lock lane | Runner / build UX | Running `npm run build` and a frozen-runner command in parallel can expose a transient onefile cache path failure. | Frozen runner cache refresh should be atomic or runner commands should wait/retry when the cache is being rebuilt. | Repaired on 2026-06-28 by moving the onefile launcher to an atomic extraction protocol: payload extraction now takes a per-payload lock, writes into a unique staging directory, publishes readiness only after the payload is complete, and lets concurrent runners wait/retry against the same cache root instead of crashing on a half-refreshed tree. The launcher also now honors `ATM_ONEFILE_CACHE_ROOT`, which makes isolated validation and cache hygiene deterministic. Regression coverage lives in `scripts/validate-onefile-release.ts`, and `scripts/validate-onefile-budget.ts --json` now also reports extraction-lock handoff results alongside startup timing. | Keep extraction-lock wait coverage in `scripts/validate-onefile-release.ts` and preserve the lock-handoff summary in `scripts/validate-onefile-budget.ts`; future onefile cache changes must not reintroduce partial-tree visibility during rebuild. |

| ATM-BUG-2026-06-15-008 | 2026-06-15 | AI-Atomic-Framework | Bug | High | Fixed in this cleanup commit | Team Agents | `team plan` / `team validate` reject imported cross-repo planning tasks whose `scopePaths` are absolute 3KLife paths, so Phase 0 planning tasks cannot start through Team Agents even after broker cleanup. | Team Agents should normalize or classify cross-repo planning paths before building `file.write` leases, or choose a read-only/planning recipe that does not request unsafe writes. | Fixed by deriving Team Agents write scope from target repo paths only: `targetAllowedFiles` is authoritative when present, target-root absolute paths normalize to repo-relative write leases, and planning-repo absolute paths become read-only planning context instead of `file.write` lease paths. `node --strip-types scripts/validate-team-agents.ts --case permission-lease` now creates a temp target/planning repo fixture and proves planning absolute paths do not raise `ATM_TEAM_WRITE_SCOPE_TRAVERSAL` or emit an empty `file.write` lease. | Keep the cross-repo planning fixture in `scripts/validate-team-agents.ts`; future Team Agents scope changes must preserve target-write fail-closed behavior while allowing planning-only absolute context. |
| ATM-BUG-2026-06-15-009 | 2026-06-15 | AI-Atomic-Framework | Optimization | High | Fixed in 2026-06-28 claim-readiness / latency lane | Claim / lifecycle routing | `tasks claim` and `taskflow close` for CID tasks took many rounds of reserve/promote/status probes and even a 300s `next --claim` timeout before surfacing the real blocker, so the operator path felt slow even though `path-to-atom-map.json` is only ~56 KB. | Claim should fail fast or converge quickly with one blocker summary when lifecycle state is already inconsistent; sharding should reduce shared-file contention, but it should not be needed to explain long claim latency. | Closed on 2026-06-28 by teaching `packages/cli/src/commands/next.ts` to emit a structured `claimReadiness` triage whenever `next --claim` cannot select a claimable task, including first blocker summaries for import-required, review closeout-only, dependency-closeout, and unscoped-prompt cases instead of a generic no-task answer. The same lane now emits `atm.claimLatencyTelemetry.v1` from both `next --claim` and `tasks claim`, so operators can see whether time was spent in parallel preflight, reserve/promote preparation, claim acquisition, or direction-lock writes. Focused regression coverage landed in `packages/cli/src/commands/next/__tests__/claim-readiness.test.ts`, while existing `packages/cli/src/commands/tasks/__tests__/dependency-gate.test.ts`, `packages/cli/src/commands/tasks/__tests__/lifecycle-state.test.ts`, `scripts/validate-prompt-scoped-next.ts`, and `scripts/validate-cli.ts --mode validate` continue to guard the broader claim route. | Keep the structured `claimReadiness` envelope and `atm.claimLatencyTelemetry.v1` attached to claim entrypoints; future claim / close routing changes must preserve first-blocker surfacing before operators fall back to manual reserve/promote/status probe loops. |
| ATM-BUG-2026-06-15-010 | 2026-06-15 | AI-Atomic-Framework | Optimization | High | Fixed in historical-batch evidence lane | Historical evidence / taskflow close | Completed multi-task delivery packages currently force operators to close or evidence tasks one by one, even when the real delivery landed as a coherent commit bundle with shared validators. This creates noisy after-the-fact evidence work and makes it hard to distinguish historical attestation from original live evidence. | ATM should support a governed historical batch evidence envelope: one delivery commit range, one validator set, one artifact manifest, and per-task scoped evidence slices that preserve each task acceptance boundary. The evidence must be marked historical, not fresh live execution. | Source reality now satisfies this contract: `packages/cli/src/commands/evidence.ts` implements `evidence historical-batch`, `packages/cli/src/commands/taskflow.ts` and `tasks close` consume `--historical-batch`, `docs/governance/historical-batch-evidence.md` documents the operator flow, and `packages/cli/src/commands/tasks/__tests__/historical-delivery.test.ts` plus `packages/cli/src/commands/taskflow/__tests__/taskflow-dryrun.spec.ts` cover complete slices, unmatched safeguards, envelope staging, and per-task close readiness. | Keep historical-batch command/spec/docs/tests aligned; remaining partial-slice disposition is separately tracked by `ATM-BUG-2026-06-16-014`. |
| ATM-BUG-2026-06-16-011 | 2026-06-16 | AI-Atomic-Framework | Product gap | High | Fixed in 2026-06-28 deferred-governance diagnosis lane | Pre-commit governance / framework-mode | Pre-commit governance blocks can fail a legitimate framework-repo commit because `framework claim` / direction-lock state is missing, even when the diff content, validators, and historical governance intent are otherwise correct. The hook currently treats governance timing gaps as a hard commit failure instead of distinguishing them from content-integrity failures. | Framework-repo pre-commit should surface a precise deferred-governance diagnosis, and historical-batch or closeback flows should have an explicit, governed path to satisfy or defer framework claim / direction-lock requirements without forcing blanket `--no-verify`. | Closed on 2026-06-28 by teaching `packages/cli/src/commands/hook.ts` to classify pre-commit failures into governance-state versus content-validation lanes instead of flattening everything into one generic block. `failureEnvelope` now exposes `governanceStateFailures`, `contentValidationFailures`, and `deferredGovernanceCandidate`, while governance-only failures surface the dedicated hook code `ATM_HOOK_PRE_COMMIT_DEFERRED_GOVERNANCE_REQUIRED` so operators can tell that the staged content is not failing validation and the remaining blocker is claim/governance timing. Regression coverage was added to `scripts/validate-git-hooks-enforcement.ts`, which now stages a framework-critical file in a fixture repo, forces validator success, and proves the hook reports the deferred-governance marker instead of a generic content-failure-only diagnosis. | Keep the deferred-governance split in `packages/cli/src/commands/hook.ts` and the fixture-backed regression in `scripts/validate-git-hooks-enforcement.ts`; future hook refactors must preserve a first-class governance-state diagnosis whenever the staged content is otherwise validator-clean. |
| ATM-BUG-2026-06-16-012 | 2026-06-16 | AI-Atomic-Framework | Optimization | High | Fixed in 2026-06-28 historical-batch validator attestation lane | Historical batch evidence / validators | `taskflow close --historical-batch` can use a batch envelope slice, but each task close still needs fresh per-task `evidence run` validator records. `evidence run --recent-run` records `historical-reference`, which is useful for diagnosis but not enough for close, so a 4-card batch still reruns expensive validators multiple times. | A batch close wave should support one fresh validator execution set with signed per-task validator slices, preserving task-specific acceptance while avoiding repeated `npm test` / `typecheck` runs for the same delivery commit. | Closed on 2026-06-28 by splitting historical-batch task evidence into two coordinated records inside `packages/cli/src/commands/evidence.ts`: the delivery provenance record stays `historical-reference`, while a second `atm.historicalBatchValidatorAttestation.v1` record carries the same proof-backed `commandRuns` plus reusable fresh validator passes for that task slice. This keeps historical delivery semantics intact but lets close/evidence gates consume one shared fresh validator execution wave without rerunning the same validator per task. Regression coverage now lives in `packages/cli/src/commands/tasks/__tests__/historical-delivery.test.ts`, which proves the historical slice is still historical-reference while `verifyTaskEvidence(..., gate: 'close')` passes from the fresh attestation slice alone. Validation also re-ran `scripts/validate-governance-commands.ts --mode validate` to keep the broader evidence/governance surface green. | Preserve the dual-record contract: historical delivery provenance must remain historical-reference, while reusable same-wave validator proof stays fresh and command-backed. Future evidence refactors must not collapse these back into one stale record or force per-task validator reruns after a batch envelope already executed them successfully. |
| ATM-BUG-2026-06-16-013 | 2026-06-16 | AI-Atomic-Framework | Bug | High | Fixed in `5f1a4548` | Historical batch evidence / commit bundle | `taskflow close --historical-batch` writes per-task closure bundles but does not stage the referenced historical batch envelope, leaving `.atm/history/evidence/historical-batches/<batch>.json` untracked while closure packets reference it. | The close commit bundle should include the referenced historical batch envelope, or create a governed batch-envelope commit before task-level closure packets can reference it. | After closing `TASK-CID-0103`, `git status --short` still showed `?? .atm/history/evidence/historical-batches/hist-batch-2026-06-16T01-40-43-634Z.json`; closure output referenced that same batch path as the source of the slice. Fast repair `5f1a4548` added envelope staging and dogfood dry-runs for `TASK-CID-0105` / `TASK-CID-0107` showed the batch envelope in `governedCommitBundle.targetRepo.stageFiles`. | Keep regression coverage in `packages/cli/src/commands/taskflow/__tests__/taskflow-dryrun.spec.ts`. |
| ATM-BUG-2026-06-16-014 | 2026-06-16 | AI-Atomic-Framework | Product gap | Medium | Fixed in historical-batch diagnostic disposition lane | Historical batch evidence / partial slices | Historical batch import can leave unclosed partial or diagnostic-only task slices as untracked `.atm/history/tasks`, evidence, and task-events, while completed slices close cleanly. The operator previously had no clear governed command to archive, abandon, or commit diagnostic-only slices without pretending they are done. | Batch evidence should provide an explicit partial-slice disposition: keep diagnostic evidence, abandon with reason, or remove generated diagnostic evidence through a governed cleanup path. Close-ready slices must remain fail-closed to taskflow close. | Fixed by `node atm.mjs evidence historical-batch-finalize`: it reads the batch envelope, refuses `okToCloseTask: true` slices, records `atm.historicalBatchTaskSliceDisposition.v1` in the envelope, appends audit evidence for `keep-diagnostic`/`abandon`, and supports `remove-evidence` that removes only task evidence records referencing that batch. | Keep `packages/cli/src/commands/tasks/__tests__/historical-delivery.test.ts` coverage for approved diagnostic batch finalization, `remove-evidence` cleanup, and close-ready finalize refusal. |
| ATM-BUG-2026-06-18-015 | 2026-06-18 | AI-Atomic-Framework | Bug | High | Fixed in 2026-06-28 branch queue validation lane | Git governance / multi-agent commit lane | Two Codex agents can both pass local governance checks, then collide at final `git commit` with `fatal: cannot lock ref 'HEAD'` because another agent moved `HEAD` between wrapper preflight and commit execution. The wrapper surfaces the raw failure, but ATM does not yet serialize the final branch-tip mutation through a steward lane or retry on safe fast-forward drift. | When governed commits target the same branch concurrently, ATM should funnel the final branch-tip mutation through a serialized steward lane or equivalent commit queue. At minimum, the wrapper should detect `HEAD` drift, re-evaluate branch state, and emit a first-class queue/retry path instead of a raw Git race. | The current source now satisfies that contract: `packages/cli/src/commands/git-governance.ts` serializes final commit mutation through `withBranchCommitQueueLock(...)`, emits `ATM_GIT_COMMIT_BRANCH_QUEUE_BUSY` / `ATM_GIT_COMMIT_BRANCH_QUEUE_RACE`, records `atm.branchCommitQueueEvidence.v1`, and explicitly detects raw `cannot lock ref 'HEAD'` races.
